href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;">Part of the <b><a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008 Atlantic hurricane season</a></b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="display:none">\n<td colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hurricane Gustav</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xca\x8a/: \'oo\' in \'foot\'">\xca\x8a</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: \'a\' in \'father\'">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">v</span></span>/</a></span></span>) was the second most destructive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008 Atlantic hurricane season</a>. The seventh <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a>, third <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a>, and second major hurricane of the season, Gustav caused serious damage and <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(person)" title="Casualty (person)">casualties</a> in Haiti, the Dominican Republic, Jamaica, the Cayman Islands, Cuba and the United States. Gustav caused at least $6.6\xc2\xa0billion (2008\xc2\xa0USD) in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>It formed on the morning of August 25, 2008, about 260 miles (420\xc2\xa0km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and rapidly strengthened into a tropical storm that afternoon and into a hurricane early on August 26. Later that day it made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> near the Haitian town of <a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">Jacmel</a>. It inundated Jamaica and ravaged Western Cuba and then steadily moved across the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Once into the Gulf, Gustav gradually weakened because of increased wind shear and dry air. It weakened to a Category 2 hurricane late on August 31, and remained at that intensity until landfall on the morning of September 1 near <a href="/wiki/Cocodrie,_Louisiana" title="Cocodrie, Louisiana">Cocodrie, Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup> Weakening continued, and Gustav weakened to a tropical storm that evening and to a tropical depression the next day as it meandered around the south-central US. The weak system became extratropical on September 4 and was absorbed by another low on September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In total, an estimated 153 deaths had been attributed to Gustav in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. Damage in the U.S. totaled to $4.3\xc2\xa0billion (2008\xc2\xa0USD)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SeasonSummary_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-SeasonSummary-5">[5]</a></sup> with additional damage of $2.1\xc2\xa0billion in Cuba<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMOCuba2008_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMOCuba2008-6">[6]</a></sup> and $210\xc2\xa0million in damage in Jamaica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCCuba_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCuba-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Gustav" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Gustav">Meteorological history of Hurricane Gustav</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="831" data-file-width="1024" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Gustav_2008_track.png/220px-Gustav_2008_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Gustav_2008_track.png/330px-Gustav_2008_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Gustav_2008_track.png/440px-Gustav_2008_track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Gustav formed out of a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that had previously produced t-rain and <a href="/wiki/Squall" title="Squall">squalls</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>. It developed well-defined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone#Banding" title="Tropical Cyclone">curved bands</a> and briefly exhibited an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a>. The NHC designated it <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression" title="Tropical Depression">Tropical Depression</a> Seven and dispatched a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_hunter" title="Hurricane hunter">hurricane hunter</a> aircraft to investigate the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc001_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc001-8">[8]</a></sup> At the time, the system had a well-defined <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> in all but the southeast and southwest quadrant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc001_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-disc001-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wndspd01_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-wndspd01-9">[9]</a></sup> and data from the hurricane-hunter aircraft confirmed that the tropical depression had strengthened into a tropical storm, which was soon designated Tropical Storm Gustav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_aug25_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-update_aug25-10">[10]</a></sup> A brief period of disorganization<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> proved to be temporary as a well-defined eye wall formed that same night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc04_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc04-12">[12]</a></sup> In the early hours of August 26, as the storm approached Haiti\'s southwestern peninsula,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public04a_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-public04a-13">[13]</a></sup> another hurricane hunter aircraft confirmed what forecasters already suspected\xe2\x80\x94that Gustav had strengthened into a hurricane with winds topping 90\xc2\xa0mph (150\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_aug26_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-update_aug26-14">[14]</a></sup> Before reaching Haiti, its satellite presentation continued to intensify, a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> became more prominent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc05_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc05-15">[15]</a></sup> and the minimum central pressure fell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc06_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc06-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5600" data-file-width="4400" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg/220px-Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg/330px-Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg/440px-Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustavat1Landfall08.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Gustav making landfall in Haiti on August 25</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hurricane Gustav regained a pronounced eye as it made landfall on Haiti, with 75\xc2\xa0mph (121\xc2\xa0km/h) winds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc07_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc07-17">[17]</a></sup> near the town of Jacmel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public06a_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-public06a-18">[18]</a></sup> As the hurricane moved over Haiti\'s mountainous terrain its circulation was disrupted<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc07_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-disc07-17">[17]</a></sup> and it lost a little strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public08_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-public08-19">[19]</a></sup> Although downgraded to a tropical storm, it still had a pronounced eye in its mid- and upper-level structures. Its outflow improved throughout the night of August 26,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc08_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc08-20">[20]</a></sup> and the system was not very disrupted when it moved back over water into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Gon%C3%A2ve" title="Gulf of Gon\xc3\xa2ve">Gulf of Gon\xc3\xa2ve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc09_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc09-21">[21]</a></sup> However, the storm\'s movement slowed, and continued interaction with nearby Haiti, combined with the incursion of mid-level dry air from the northeast, resulted in further weakening during the day on August 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public11_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-public11-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc12_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc12-23">[23]</a></sup> The storm began a west-southwesterly movement that brought it closer to Jamaica. On the morning of August 28 it was found that, overnight, Gustav had either reformed farther to the south or had moved farther to the south than previously thought. The storm was also found to have restrengthened nearly to hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public14_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-public14-24">[24]</a></sup> It then was upgraded to a hurricane again during the late afternoon of August 29. At 11:00 a.m <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Daylight_Time" title="Eastern Daylight Time">EDT</a> (1500\xc2\xa0UTC) on August 30, as Gustav neared the west end of Cuba, it was upgraded to a Category\xc2\xa03 hurricane on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public22A_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-public22A-25">[25]</a></sup> with sustained winds near 125\xc2\xa0mph (205\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public22A_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-public22A-25">[25]</a></sup> Gustav continued its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> trend, and three hours later, it had already reached Category\xc2\xa04 strength. Gustav\'s maximum sustained winds had reached 155\xc2\xa0mph (250\xc2\xa0km/h)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public25_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-public25-26">[26]</a></sup> with a minimum pressure of 941\xc2\xa0millibars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public25a_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-public25a-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On August 30 Gustav made landfall twice on <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>: first, on <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a> and then on the mainland near the community of <a href="/wiki/Los_Palacios" title="Los Palacios">Los Palacios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo_Province" title="Pinar del R\xc3\xado Province">Pinar del R\xc3\xado Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cuba_landfall_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cuba_landfall-28">[28]</a></sup> By the early hours of August 31, Gustav entered the Gulf of Mexico with maximum sustained winds of 135\xc2\xa0mph (217\xc2\xa0km/h) and minimum central pressure of 958\xc2\xa0millibars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public26_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-public26-29">[29]</a></sup> During August 31, the storm moved in a northwest direction slightly losing its strength (despite passing over a shortened <a href="/wiki/Loop_Current" title="Loop Current">Loop Current</a>) with sustained winds at 115\xc2\xa0mph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public28_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-public28-30">[30]</a></sup> On the evening of August 31, Gustav weakened to a Category 2 hurricane and remained at such intensity until landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup> Gustav made landfall along the Louisiana coast with 105\xc2\xa0mph (170\xc2\xa0km/h) winds near Cocodrie,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public032_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-public032-31">[31]</a></sup> at about 9:30 a.m <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Daylight_Time" title="Central Daylight Time">CDT</a> (1430\xc2\xa0UTC). By 10\xc2\xa0pm CDT, Gustav had been downgraded to a Tropical Storm with winds of 60\xc2\xa0mph (95\xc2\xa0km/h) about 20\xc2\xa0miles (30\xc2\xa0km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, Louisiana<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public34_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-public34-32">[32]</a></sup> and by 4\xc2\xa0am CDT on September 2 Gustav had diminished to a Tropical Depression with a threat of severe flooding in the lower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_Valley" title="Mississippi Valley">Mississippi Valley</a> and eastern Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public35_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-public35-33">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hispaniola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Immediately upon the storm\'s designation as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_depression" title="Tropical depression">tropical depression</a> it was expected to strengthen into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> and strike the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc001_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-disc001-8">[8]</a></sup> shared by the Dominican Republic on the east and Haiti on the west. Tropical storm warnings were issued from the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> to the Haitian coast south of Port-au-Prince. A tropical storm watch was issued for the Haitian coast, north of Port-au-Prince to the northern border with the Dominican Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Hours later, when Gustav was upgraded to a tropical storm, the tropical storm warning was upgraded to a hurricane warning and the tropical storm watch was upgraded to a hurricane warning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Aug_26_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Aug_26-36">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Haitian government ordered emergency shelters to prepare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_Tribune_Aug26_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Tribune_Aug26-37">[37]</a></sup> The country is particularly vulnerable to floods and landslides as rainfall <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">runs off</a> its largely <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforested</a> mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Aug_26_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Aug_26-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_UK_Aug26_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_UK_Aug26-38">[38]</a></sup> The government issued a red alert<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_UK_Aug26_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_UK_Aug26-38">[38]</a></sup> and advised the population to take precautions, but few Haitians took heed. Fair weather led many to doubt whether a hurricane was even approaching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_Tribune_Aug26_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Tribune_Aug26-37">[37]</a></sup> American Airlines canceled all of its flights into and out of Port-au-Prince on August 26, stranding travelers hoping to escape the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_Tribune_Aug26_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Tribune_Aug26-37">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica_and_Cayman_Islands">Jamaica and Cayman Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Jamaica and Cayman Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4791" data-file-width="4817" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg/220px-Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg/330px-Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg/440px-Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_29_August_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Gustav, just after making landfall in Jamaica, August 29</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On August 25, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">Carnival Cruise Lines</a> diverted one of its ships from <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">Montego Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> in order to avoid the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_Tribune_Aug26_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Tribune_Aug26-37">[37]</a></sup> Jamaica\'s <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Disaster_Preparedness_and_Emergency_Management" title="Office of Disaster Preparedness and Emergency Management">Office of Disaster Preparedness and Emergency Management</a> (ODPEM) readied response systems in anticipation of Hurricane Gustav affecting the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radio_Jam_Aug26_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radio_Jam_Aug26-39">[39]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, a hurricane watch was issued at 6\xc2\xa0pm August 25 and upgraded that to a warning on 6\xc2\xa0pm August 27. Banks and non-essential government services were closed Friday to allow residents to prepare. Extra flights were organized to get tourists off the island and, per usual practice, further visits were banned until the All Clear was given. Stores and gas stations were busy and each district office offered free plywood to protect windows and residents hurried about to secure their business interests and property.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GustavCuba.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="501" data-file-width="680" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/GustavCuba.gif/220px-GustavCuba.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/GustavCuba.gif/330px-GustavCuba.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/GustavCuba.gif/440px-GustavCuba.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GustavCuba.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nInfrared Satellite loops of Hurricane Gustav crossing western Cuba as a major category 4 storm.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>60,000 were evacuated overnight on August 29 from Cuba\'s western coasts. Gustav was projected to strike Cuba on the afternoon of August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Additional evacuations were ordered on the afternoon of August 30 as Gustav strengthened to a strong Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane, particularly in the low-lying Pinar del R\xc3\xado Province where 190,000 were evacuated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> On Monday, September 1, Cuban officials reported that Gustav\'s 155\xc2\xa0mph (249\xc2\xa0km/h) winds damaged or destroyed 90,000 homes in Pinar del R\xc3\xado, and knocked down 80 high-tension towers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The combined damage estimate from Gustav and the subsequent hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">Ike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paloma" title="Hurricane Paloma">Paloma</a> is about $9.4\xc2\xa0billion (USD), with about 2.1\xc2\xa0billion of that from Gustav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCCuba_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCuba-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On August 31, the NHC predicted with 45% probability that Gustav would remain at Category\xc2\xa03 or above on September 1. This influenced preparations, although in fact Gustav had dropped just below the Category\xc2\xa03 threshold to Category\xc2\xa02 by landfall, and Category\xc2\xa01 shortly afterwards.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg/220px-RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg/330px-RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg/440px-RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RinkNOLAStillPerkinBoards.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBuilding being boarded up in <a href="/wiki/Uptown_New_Orleans" title="Uptown New Orleans">Uptown New Orleans</a>, August 28</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On the morning of August 26, with Gustav still over Haiti, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> emergency preparedness officials met several times to discuss predictions that Gustav would reach the state as a major hurricane in three to five days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_26_gearsup_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA_26_gearsup-44">[44]</a></sup> Several areas of Louisiana planned for evacuations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC142_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC142-45">[45]</a></sup> Several parishes in the <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> area announced plans for voluntary evacuations beginning Saturday, August 30. New Orleans Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ray_Nagin" title="Ray Nagin">Ray Nagin</a> said that it was possible thousands of people who need city help could start leaving on Saturday, as the first wave of a full-scale evacuation. Later, he ordered the mandatory evacuation of the whole of New Orleans commencing on the morning of August 31, calling Gustav "the storm of the century\xc2\xa0... the mother of all storms."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC142_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC142-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-evacuate_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-evacuate-46">[46]</a></sup> On August 31, Nagin also declared a dusk-to-dawn <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a> and the cessation of city assistance in evacuations by the afternoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Bush_dangerous_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Bush_dangerous-47">[47]</a></sup> By that afternoon, 1.9\xc2\xa0million people had evacuated southern Louisiana, with 200,000 being residents of New Orleans alone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_1.1M_evacuated_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA_1.1M_evacuated-48">[48]</a></sup> making it the largest evacuation in the history of Louisiana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Officials had finalized evacuation plans, which proposed assisted evacuations as early as August 29: <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">Contraflow lane reversal</a> on all major highways, and 700\xc2\xa0buses to help move evacuees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLA_26_alert_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA_26_alert-50">[50]</a></sup> For those evacuees in need of shelter, the state government secured tens of thousands of shelter beds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26_landfall_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_26_landfall-51">[51]</a></sup> Wary of repeating <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of government response to Hurricane Katrina">the mistakes of Hurricane Katrina</a>, authorities chose not to use the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Superdome" title="Louisiana Superdome">Louisiana Superdome</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Convention_Center" title="New Orleans Convention Center">New Orleans Convention Center</a> as emergency shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_26_skittish_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_26_skittish-52">[52]</a></sup> The following day, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Louisiana" title="Governor of Louisiana">Louisiana governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jindal" title="Bobby Jindal">Bobby Jindal</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>, activating between 3,000 and 8,000\xc2\xa0members of the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_National_Guard" title="Louisiana National Guard">Louisiana National Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_state_of_emergency_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-LA_state_of_emergency-53">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="536" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG/220px-Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG/330px-Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG/440px-Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louisiana_National_Guard_Adj_General_Press_Conference.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMaj. Gen. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bennett_C._Landreneau" title="Bennett C. Landreneau">Bennett C. Landreneau</a> (center), <a href="/wiki/Adjutant_general" title="Adjutant general">adjutant general</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Army_National_Guard" title="Louisiana Army National Guard">Louisiana Army National Guard</a>, speaks to reporters about the Guard\'s preparation for Gustav in Louisiana on August 28.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mayor of New Orleans Ray Nagin shortened his appearance at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denver,_Colorado" title="Denver, Colorado">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, to assist in preparations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The residents of low-lying <a href="/wiki/Grand_Isle,_Louisiana" title="Grand Isle, Louisiana">Grand Isle, Louisiana</a>, were under a voluntary evacuation order beginning August 29. Traditionally, the community is one of the first to vacate when tropical storms threaten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC142_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC142-45">[45]</a></sup> Residents of lower <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">Cameron Parish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, were also given a voluntary evacuation order on August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Mandatory evacuation orders have since been given. In <a href="/wiki/Plaquemines_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Plaquemines Parish, Louisiana">Plaquemines Parish</a>, Parish President <a href="/wiki/Billy_Nungesser" title="Billy Nungesser">Billy Nungesser</a> flew in a helicopter counting the number of vessels and barges that potentially would be a safety issue to people, property, and the levee system during a hurricane. Parish officials called the owners of about 150 vessels and told them to move the vessels or the parish would sink them. 70 of the 150 were sunk, some by the parish, some by the owners. <a class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080918040737/http://www.wwltv.com/topstories/stories/wwl091608mlplaq.82dc39c1.html" rel="nofollow">[1]</a> Also, parish officials started a last-ditch effort to save <a href="/wiki/Belle_Chasse,_Louisiana" title="Belle Chasse, Louisiana">Belle Chasse</a> by constructing a sand levee across <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Highway_23" title="Louisiana Highway 23">Louisiana Highway 23</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWL_Plaquemines_1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWL_Plaquemines_1-56">[56]</a></sup> Approximately eight hours later, the parish government announced the completion of the levee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWL_Plaquemines_2_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWL_Plaquemines_2-57">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> was shut to all ship traffic between the Gulf of Mexico and New Orleans on August 30. Pilots at Lake Charles in west Louisiana, and Sabine Pass in east Texas, also were making plans as of August 30 to halt traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">Tulane University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_New_Orleans" title="Loyola University New Orleans">Loyola University New Orleans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Orleans" title="University of New Orleans">University of New Orleans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Xavier_University_of_Louisiana" title="Xavier University of Louisiana">Xavier University of Louisiana</a> all closed their campuses for the entire week but resumed classes on the following Monday of September 8, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tulane_emergency_response_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tulane_emergency_response-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Louisiana_at_Lafayette" title="University of Louisiana at Lafayette">University of Louisiana at Lafayette</a> also canceled classes for September 2 and 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> as did <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_State_University" title="Louisiana State University">Louisiana State University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge_Community_College" title="Baton Rouge Community College">Baton Rouge Community College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRCC_closed_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRCC_closed-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On September 1, Plaquemines Parish officials asked the residents of <a href="/wiki/Braithwaite,_Louisiana" title="Braithwaite, Louisiana">Braithwaite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> to leave, as levee failure was considered imminent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Braithwaite_levee_evacs_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Braithwaite_levee_evacs-64">[64]</a></sup> FEMA had estimated there were only about 10,000\xc2\xa0people left in New Orleans on September 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_events">Local events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Local events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>One major sporting event was directly affected by the disaster preparations. On August 30, Louisiana State University (LSU) opened <a href="/wiki/2008_LSU_Tigers_football_team" title="2008 LSU Tigers football team">its 2008\xc2\xa0football season</a> against <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_State_Mountaineers_football" title="Appalachian State Mountaineers football">Appalachian State</a>. The originally scheduled kickoff time of 4\xc2\xa0pm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">CDT</a> would have conflicted with the start of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraflow" title="Contraflow">contraflow</a> lane reversal, and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10_in_Louisiana" title="Interstate 10 in Louisiana">Interstate 10</a> is a key evacuation route through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a>. Accordingly, LSU moved kickoff to 10\xc2\xa0am CDT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LSU-App_State_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-LSU-App_State-66">[66]</a></sup> A college football game between <a href="/wiki/Nicholls_State_University" title="Nicholls State University">Nicholls State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_State_University" title="New Mexico State University">New Mexico State University</a>, scheduled for September 4, was canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The Triple-A baseball <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Zephyrs" title="New Orleans Zephyrs">New Orleans Zephyrs</a> cancelled the final three games of their season because of the impending approach of Gustav and evacuation preparations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">New Orleans Saints</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) proceeded with plans to evacuate from New Orleans and headed to <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, where they practiced at <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Oil_Stadium" title="Lucas Oil Stadium">Lucas Oil Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The Saints returned to New Orleans to play their first home game as scheduled on Sunday, September 7, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> 24\xe2\x80\x9320.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hotel and business closures related to Gustav had impact on New Orleans\' <a class="external text" href="http://www.southerndecadence.net/" rel="nofollow">Southern Decadence</a> celebrations, which were scheduled for August 27 through September 1, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washblade_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-washblade-72">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas">Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2481" data-file-width="3870" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg/225px-FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg/338px-FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg/450px-FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_Admin_with_other_officials_preparing_for_Gustav.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) Administrator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Paulison" title="David Paulison">David Paulison</a> (center) with various United States\' federal officials and other response leaders on August 30.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a> activated 5,000 members of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Military_Forces" title="Texas Military Forces">Texas Military Forces</a> on August 29 in response to the possible crisis, in addition to preparations made by other agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> As of August 29, other preparations in Texas to deal with Gustav and its effects were implemented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Some evacuees were being placed in Northeast Texas, including in <a href="/wiki/Dallas_County,_Texas" title="Dallas County, Texas">Dallas County</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarrant_County" title="Tarrant County">Tarrant County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_Texas" title="Tyler, Texas">Tyler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">Harris County</a>, Texas, the administrative County Judge <a href="/wiki/Ed_Emmett" title="Ed Emmett">Ed Emmett</a> said that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Astrodome" title="Reliant Astrodome">Reliant Astrodome</a> will not be used as a shelter for evacuees if Hurricane Gustav hits New Orleans because Houston is also vulnerable to Hurricane Gustav. Emmett said that it would make more sense to evacuate to a more inland area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Voluntary evacuations of <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Texas" title="Jefferson County, Texas">Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Texas" title="Orange County, Texas">Orange</a> Counties started on August 30 with mandatory evacuations in the two counties started on August 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Also, the Texas Governor deployed other assets to help handle the oncoming disaster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mississippi_and_Alabama">Mississippi and Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mississippi and Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On August 27, requests and orders began for evacuations along the Mississippi Gulf Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> All schools in <a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Mississippi" title="Harrison County, Mississippi">Harrison County\'s</a> five public school districts were closed until September 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Several schools in Pearl River County were also confirmed closed until September 2. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Mississippi" title="University of Southern Mississippi">University of Southern Mississippi</a> was closed on September 2, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Alcorn_State_University" title="Alcorn State University">Alcorn State University</a>.</p>\n<p>Much of the <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> National Guard was mobilized to assist evacuees from the other states. Governor Bob Riley called for mandatory evacuation of Dauphin Island, Plash Island, Gulf Shores, as well as everything south of Fort Morgan Road, Gulf Shores on August 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Regional_Airport" title="Mobile Regional Airport">Mobile Regional Airport</a> closed on August 31, and remained closed September 1. It is reopened September 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gustav_School.2FBusiness_Closings_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gustav_School.2FBusiness_Closings-82">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bankhead_Tunnel" title="Bankhead Tunnel">Bankhead Tunnel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, closed on August 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gustav_School.2FBusiness_Closings_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gustav_School.2FBusiness_Closings-82">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Multistate_agencies">Multistate agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Multistate agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On Friday, August 29 several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rural_Water" title="Rural Water">state rural waters associations</a> activated their Water Agency Response Networks to prepare for Gustav\xe2\x80\x99s landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> WARN systems are agreements between rural water associations and government agencies in neighboring states that coordinate the response to large water emergencies. Water technicians and trailers of portable generators, pumps, spare parts and testing equipment were readied along the Gulf Coast and neighboring states to respond to the emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table border="1" class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin:0 1em 0.5em 1em;">\n<caption>Deaths by country</caption>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a></td>\n<td>77</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a></td>\n<td>8</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a></td>\n<td>15</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td>\n<td>53</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Total</td>\n<td>153</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Operationally, Gustav went from a tropical depression to a hurricane in 14\xc2\xa0hours, tying <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Humberto_(2007)" title="Hurricane Humberto (2007)">Hurricane Humberto\'s</a> record of 14\xc2\xa0hours, although this may be disputed in post-season analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the aftermath, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_government" title="Canadian government">Canadian government</a> sent a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-17_Globemaster_III" title="C-17 Globemaster III">C-17</a> airlifter, with a medical team, from <a href="/wiki/CFB_Trenton" title="CFB Trenton">CFB Trenton</a> to assist in the evacuation of New Orleans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" title="C-130 Hercules">C-130 Hercules</a> airlift planes from <a href="/wiki/Greenwood,_Nova_Scotia" title="Greenwood, Nova Scotia">Greenwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> and from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winnipeg,_Manitoba" title="Winnipeg, Manitoba">Winnipeg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> sent <a href="/wiki/HMS_Iron_Duke_(F234)" title="HMS Iron Duke (F234)">HMS <i>Iron Duke</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/RFA_Wave_Ruler_(A390)" title="RFA Wave Ruler (A390)">RFA <i>Wave Ruler</i></a> to provide emergency assistance and assess the damage caused by Gustav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> provided canned water to affected residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anheuser_Busch_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anheuser_Busch-89">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> announced it would send 4 cargo planes with tents, construction materials, food, and essential supplies to Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispaniola_2">Hispaniola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hispaniola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right;">65.0</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.56</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fox_(1952)" title="Hurricane Fox (1952)">Fox 1952</a></td>\n<td>Ouanaminthe</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-97">[97]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_truck.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165"
