1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Gustav_truck.jpg/440px-Gustav_truck.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_truck.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA truck buried under rubble in Haiti</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the Dominican Republic, a landslide in a rural area killed eight people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Two people were injured. Government authorities said that some 67,255 persons were evacuated and more than 1,239 homes were damaged with 12 destroyed. 50 communities were isolated by the flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNOCHA_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNOCHA-99">[99]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Gustav made landfall in Haiti at approximately 1\xc2\xa0pm EDT on August 26, about 10\xc2\xa0miles (16\xc2\xa0km) west of the city of Jacmel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti_Landfall_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti_Landfall-100">[100]</a></sup> While inland, Gustav\'s rains triggered a landslide in the community of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Benet,_Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Benet, Haiti (page does not exist)">Benet</a> which killed one person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Two more were killed in southwestern Haiti when their house collapsed. Another two deaths were caused by an explosion inside a house, thought to be possibly related to Hurricane Gustav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The southern town of Jacmel, where the hurricane made landfall, was bisected by floodwaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_26_landfall_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_26_landfall-51">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to Haiti\'s National Director of Civil Protection, 77\xc2\xa0people died as a result of the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup> Some 2,100 houses were destroyed and another 8,150 damaged, causing an estimated 7,200\xc2\xa0people to live in temporary shelters, including churches, community centers and schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNOCHA_1_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNOCHA_1-103">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In Jamaica, 15 deaths were reported after Gustav swept through the area as a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup> Flash flooding was also reported on the island as a result of Gustav\'s heavy rains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The banana sector in the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Saint Thomas Parish, Jamaica">St. Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mary_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Saint Mary Parish, Jamaica">St. Mary</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portland_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Portland Parish, Jamaica">Portland</a> suffered significant damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The Hope River Bridge linking the capital <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a> with the eastern reaches of the city including Harbour View and St. Thomas collapsed and the Georgia bridge in Portland was destroyed. Jamaica\'s government ministry initially estimated US$41.8\xc2\xa0million in damage to the road infrastructure in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Total damage in Jamaica was estimated at $210\xc2\xa0million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cayman_Islands">Cayman Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cayman Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the Cayman Islands, Gustav\'s heavy rains and storm surge flooded the streets of <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>, the smaller easternmost "Sister Islands" in the chain. More than 1,100\xc2\xa0people spent the night in government shelters in the three islands as high waves and heavy winds battered the chain, the National Emergency Operations Center said in a statement. Most people waited out the storm in private homes or hotels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_2">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="2200" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg/200px-Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg/300px-Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg/400px-Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_churned_waters_off_Cuba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWaters churned up by Hurricane Gustav off the coast of Northern Cuba</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On Saturday August 30, 2008, Gustav made landfall on mainland Cuba near the community of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Palacios,_Cuba" title="Los Palacios, Cuba">Los Palacios</a> in Pinar del R\xc3\xado\xe2\x80\x94a region that produces much of the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> used to make the nation\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_cigars#Cuban_cigars" title="Cuban cigars">famed cigars</a>. In Los Palacios some 7,000 homes were roofless and many with their walls collapsed. The rice and banana farms sustained much damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>\n<p>At least 300,000\xc2\xa0people were evacuated from Gustav\'s path as 155\xc2\xa0mph (250\xc2\xa0km/h) winds toppled telephone poles and fruit trees, shattered windows and tore off the tin roofs of homes. Cuban authorities declared that Gustav is the worst hurricane to hit the country in 50\xc2\xa0years. Authorities called the storm damage the worst since 1956. The 211\xc2\xa0mph (341\xc2\xa0km/h) wind gusts registered in the city of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Paso_Real_de_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Paso Real de San Diego (page does not exist)">Paso Real de San Diego</a> were the highest in Cuba\'s history, according to the provincial newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Guerrillero_(newspaper)" title="Guerrillero (newspaper)">Guerrillero</a></i>. Winds were so strong that the weather station instruments broke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Gustav is considered Cuba\'s worst hurricane in 45\xc2\xa0years, the last hurricane that was worse than Gustav for Cuba was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flora" title="Hurricane Flora">Hurricane Flora</a> in 1963, which was the deadliest Cuban storm since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1932_Cuba_Hurricane" title="1932 Cuba Hurricane">1932 Cuba Hurricane</a>.</p>\n<p>Cuban Civil defense authorities initially stated that there were "many people injured" on Isla de la Juventud, an island of 87,000\xc2\xa0people south of the mainland. Nearly all the island\'s roads were washed out and some regions were heavily flooded. No fatalities have been reported in Cuba, despite the extreme damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cuba_landfall_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cuba_landfall-28">[28]</a></sup></p>\n<p>By September 3, Cuba\'s President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raul_Castro" title="Raul Castro">Raul Castro</a> said that 20,000 of the 25,000 houses on Isla de la Juventud were damaged. More than 90,000 homes were damaged in the western province of Pinar del R\xc3\xado according to government news agency AIN. 3,306 tobacco houses were destroyed, with 906 tons of tobacco leaves wet. More than 32,000 acres (130\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) of crops were ruined, including 7,239 acres (29.30\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) of grain and nearly 1,500 of fruit. 42,000 cans of coffee were destroyed, and 3,100 tons of grapefruit lost. 930,000 chickens had to be euthanized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Pinar del R\xc3\xado">Pinar del R\xc3\xado</a> civil defense authorities, 86,000 homes were damaged, 80 electric towers and 600 electric posts fell. Cuba\'s electric company, indicated that a total of 136 electric towers toppled over and that the electrical grid on <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a> was 100% damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In all, damage from Hurricane Gustav totaled $2.1\xc2\xa0billion in Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMOCuba_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMOCuba-112">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_2">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="920" data-file-width="762" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif/220px-Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif/330px-Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif/440px-Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_rainfall.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTotal rainfall from Gustav in the United States</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg/220px-IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg/330px-IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg/440px-IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IdeJCTerrebonneFallenHouseGustavApricot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTipped and flooded home, <a href="/wiki/Terrebonne_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana">Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Although the storm was still in its formative stages on August 26,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc05_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-disc05-15">[15]</a></sup> fears that Hurricane Gustav might eventually disrupt oil production in the Gulf of Mexico caused oil prices to rise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Aug_26_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Aug_26-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti_Landfall_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti_Landfall-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_oil_Aug26_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP_oil_Aug26-113">[113]</a></sup> On August 27, U.S. oil and natural-gas companies began evacuating personnel from their oil rigs in the Gulf of Mexico amid continued forecasts that Gustav would strengthen and move into the gulf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloom_27_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloom_27-114">[114]</a></sup> By August 30, 76.77% of oil production and 37.16% of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> production in the Gulf of Mexico had been <a href="/wiki/Shut-in_(oil_drilling)" title="Shut-in (oil drilling)">shut in</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMS_08-30_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMS_08-30-115">[115]</a></sup> By mid-day August 31, 96% of oil production had stopped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McClatchy_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchy-116">[116]</a></sup> Out at sea, one death was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup> Sunk in the Gulf as an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_reef" title="Artificial reef">artificial reef</a> in 2004, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Oriskany_(CV-34)" title="USS Oriskany (CV-34)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Oriskany</i>\xc2\xa0(CV-34)</a> shifted and was buried 10 feet deeper in the ocean floor after Gustav passed over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP2008_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP2008-117">[117]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana_2">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1700" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg/220px-Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg/330px-Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg/440px-Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008_August_31.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Gustav in the southeastern Gulf of Mexico as a Category\xc2\xa03 storm</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the state of Louisiana, 34 parishes were declared as disaster areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bushdisasterarea_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-bushdisasterarea-118">[118]</a></sup> Hurricane Gustav reached the Louisiana coast on the morning of September 1, making landfall near <a href="/wiki/Cocodrie,_Louisiana" title="Cocodrie, Louisiana">Cocodrie, Louisiana</a> (<i>see rainfall map</i>); however, at 9\xc2\xa0am wind speed at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Isle,_Louisiana" title="Grand Isle, Louisiana">Grand Isle</a> had been 115\xc2\xa0mph (185 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup> the highest eyewall speed, indicating the eyewall had traveled over 4\xc2\xa0hours along the coast. The center of the storm continued northwest across the state, so damage and deaths were widespread in many areas.</p>\n<p>48 deaths in the state of Louisiana were blamed on Hurricane Gustav. Five were due to falling trees, two due to a tornado and the rest were indirect deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>After Gustav weakened to a tropical depression, several tornadoes were spawned including one (rated EF2) that killed two near <a href="/wiki/Mamou,_Louisiana" title="Mamou, Louisiana">Mamou</a> during the early hours of September 3. The tornado also injured two others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LSREvangTor_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-LSREvangTor-120">[120]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Around 1.5\xc2\xa0million people were without power in Louisiana on September 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The state reported about 100,000\xc2\xa0people remained on the coast, after evacuation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup> Nearly 2\xc2\xa0million people had evacuated from south Louisiana in the days before Gustav\'s arrival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The city of New Orleans had the official reopening date on Thursday (Sept. 4),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRG2_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-WKRG2-122">[122]</a></sup> after crews had restored most electric power and other services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRG2_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-WKRG2-122">[122]</a></sup> Damage assessments came as residents returned to inspect their properties. Damage included numerous trees down in various locations, such as around some Marriott hotels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAhotels_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAhotels-123">[123]</a></sup> and large tree limbs were broken from oak trees along St. Charles Avenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup> Millions of smaller branches were scattered throughout neighborhoods, blown by the strong winds. Area hotels planned to reopen the week of September 8, some by Saturday, September 6 (such as the InterContinental &amp; 16 area Marriotts, which already had electricity restored).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAhotels_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAhotels-123">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup> reported on the floodwall along the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Canal" title="Industrial Canal">Industrial Canal</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor_Navigation_Canal" title="Inner Harbor Navigation Canal">Inner Harbor Navigation Canal</a>), which connects <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">Lake Pontchartrain</a> to the Mississippi River, and is susceptible to surges via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Gulf_Outlet" title="Mississippi River Gulf Outlet">Gulf Outlet</a>. High water splashed over the floodwalls onto new splash guards (designed to prevent foundation erosion), but the walls were not breached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz1_65-5"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz1-65">[65]</a></sup> Minor street flooding began in the upper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ninth_Ward_of_New_Orleans" title="Ninth Ward of New Orleans">Ninth Ward of New Orleans</a>.</p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">Baton Rouge, Louisiana</a>, it was considered to be the worst storm to hit the area since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Betsy" title="Hurricane Betsy">Hurricane Betsy</a> in 1965. An elderly couple was killed when a tree fell on the house they were temporarily staying in and 85% of the area lost power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatodaybello_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatodaybello-124">[124]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The community of <a href="/wiki/Houma,_Louisiana" title="Houma, Louisiana">Houma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, and the surrounding area in south-central Louisiana sustained extensive wind damage. The winds blew off many roofs, blew windows out of houses and knocked down many trees and left much of the region without power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup> Shingles and awnings were scattered throughout downtown Houma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup> At Ellender High in Houma, the school\'s new gym was heavily damaged, with a rear wall collapsed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-3"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup> The roof of the Houma-Terrebonne Chamber of Commerce was also blown away. Overall, the area was considered to have dodged a bullet. Had the storm come ashore farther west, the Intracoastal Waterway would have been a highway for storm surge to penetrate into the heart of Houma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-4"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup> However, flooding was relatively minor in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houma1_119-5"><a href="#cite_note-Houma1-119">[119]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Iberia,_Louisiana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg/220px-New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg/330px-New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg/440px-New_Iberia%2C_Louisiana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Iberia,_Louisiana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFlooding in front of a sign in <a href="/wiki/New_Iberia,_Louisiana" title="New Iberia, Louisiana">New Iberia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Central_Louisiana" title="Central Louisiana">Central Louisiana</a> was also hard hit. Many trees and power lines were knocked down in that region as well, and many houses sustained damage from the winds and localized flooding. Part of the roof at the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_Mall" title="Alexandria Mall">Alexandria Mall</a> collapsed. Two people died in the region\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 one was electrocuted and one had a tree crush her trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cenla1_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cenla1-125">[125]</a></sup> The area\'s water supply was also hampered as power was knocked out to most of the water wells in the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Louisiana" title="Alexandria, Louisiana">Alexandria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pineville,_Louisiana" title="Pineville, Louisiana">Pineville</a> areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTwater_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-TTwater-126">[126]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Damage and significant power outages were reported as far north as northern Louisiana, in the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_20" title="Interstate 20">Interstate 20</a> corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsStar_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewsStar-127">[127]</a></sup> Highest rainfall totals received thus far across the state include 16.37 inches (416\xc2\xa0mm) near <a href="/wiki/Bunkie,_Louisiana" title="Bunkie, Louisiana">Bunkie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> and 19.17 inches (487\xc2\xa0mm) at Barataria Bay Pass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<p>President Bush declared 34 Louisiana parishes as disaster areas and visited the area on September 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bushdisasterarea_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-bushdisasterarea-118">[118]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On Wednesday, September 3, field staff and emergency supplies from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rural_Water#Members" title="Rural Water">Arkansas Rural Water Association</a> departed to assist the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rural_Water#Members" title="Rural Water">Louisiana Rural Water Association</a> restore water and wastewater service to impacted communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Staff and supplies from other state associations, including Alabama, Mississippi and Florida went on stand-by the same day. By Friday, September 5, response teams from Arkansas, Georgia, Alabama and Mississippi were assisting efforts to restore water and wastewater service. There was little structural damage to the water infrastructure, with power loss the primary difficulty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Rural water teams provided 771 on-site technical assistance visits to 370 affected water and wastewater systems. Later, the LRWA efforts received applause from the Louisiana Joint Select Committee on Homeland Security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The LSU football team postponed their game, scheduled for September 6, against <a href="/wiki/Troy_University" title="Troy University">Troy University</a> and rescheduled it for November 15 after damage was caused to <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(LSU)" title="Tiger Stadium (LSU)">Tiger Stadium</a>. The swirling wind in the stadium tore awnings, threw team benches from the sidelines of the playing field into the stands and littered the stadium with debris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mississippi_and_Alabama_2">Mississippi and Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mississippi and Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5600" data-file-width="7200" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg/220px-Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg/330px-Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg/440px-Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustav_2008-09-01_after_landfall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Gustav just after U.S. landfall.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="400" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Gustav_Beach_Boulevard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWaves crash against a stop sign in <a href="/wiki/Bay_St._Louis,_Mississippi" title="Bay St. Louis, Mississippi">Bay St. Louis, Mississippi</a>, as Hurricane Gustav hits the Gulf Coast.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg/220px-Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg/330px-Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg/440px-Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Natchez4Sept2008EolaDamageB.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWind damage to the landmark Eola Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Natchez,_Mississippi" title="Natchez, Mississippi">Natchez, Mississippi</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The National Weather Service reported 14 confirmed tornadoes spun by Gustav from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biloxi" title="Biloxi">Biloxi</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile</a>.</p>\n<p>In Mississippi, damage from Gustav was far less severe than that caused by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>, with its 2005 storm surge of 27\xc2\xa0ft (7\xc2\xa0m); however, Gustav\'s storm surge was high as 15\xc2\xa0feet (4.5\xc2\xa0m) in places on the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Gulf_Coast" title="Mississippi Gulf Coast">Mississippi Gulf Coast</a>. Sections of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90" title="U.S. Route 90">U.S. Route 90</a> (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulfport,_MS" title="Gulfport, MS">Gulfport</a> and Biloxi) were flooded and some houses were flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS42_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS42-136">[136]</a></sup> Two people from <a href="/wiki/Metairie,_Louisiana" title="Metairie, Louisiana">Metairie, Louisiana</a> died near <a href="/wiki/Vicksburg,_Mississippi" title="Vicksburg, Mississippi">Vicksburg</a> in an automobile accident while evacuating from the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KTBS_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-KTBS-137">[137]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, scattered damage already reached multimillion-dollar levels, with the destruction of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dauphin_Island" title="Dauphin Island">Dauphin Island</a> <a href="/wiki/Berm" title="Berm">berm</a> (sand dune barrier) by storm surge waves,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGberm_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGberm-138">[138]</a></sup> flood damage to island roads &amp; homes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGberm_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGberm-138">[138]</a></sup> and extensive flooding around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayou_La_Batre" title="Bayou La Batre">Bayou La Batre</a>. The manmade sand berm took about two years to complete, and there is no official plan yet to construct another berm for Dauphin Island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGberm_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGberm-138">[138]</a></sup> which acts as a <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">barrier island</a> for the western Alabama coastline at <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Bay" title="Mobile Bay">Mobile Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGberm_138-3"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGberm-138">[138]</a></sup> A fuller assessment of damage can be expected when more residents return to the coastal areas and further <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurance_claim" title="Insurance claim">insurance claims</a> are filed.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The state of Florida was affected by both the Cuba landfall, with Gustav traveling past the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>, and the Louisiana landfall (September 1), affecting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_panhandle" title="Florida panhandle">Florida panhandle</a>, with storm surge and outer band tornadoes and thunderstorms. Several tornado warnings were issued around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pensacola" title="Pensacola">Pensacola</a> area. Panhandle beaches had rip currents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGfla_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGfla-139">[139]</a></sup> and officials in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pensacola_Beach" title="Pensacola Beach">Pensacola Beach</a> had been passing out pamphlets warning of deadly rip currents that could continue for days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKRGfla_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-WKRGfla-139">[139]</a></sup> Four people died in rip currents on Florida beaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GustavTCR_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-GustavTCR-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/USS_Oriskany_(CV-34)" title="USS Oriskany (CV-34)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Oriskany</i>\xc2\xa0(CV-34)</a>, now an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_reef" title="Artificial reef">artificial reef</a> off the coast of Pensacola, shifted 10 feet deeper leaving the flight deck at 145 feet (44\xc2\xa0m) following Gustav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP2008_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-AP2008-117">[117]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Four people died in a car accident on Interstate 20 near <a href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Georgia" title="Carrollton, Georgia">Carrollton, Georgia</a> while evacuating from Louisiana. Two other people in the car were alive and airlifted to nearby hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AJC_evac_deaths_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-AJC_evac_deaths-140">[140]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arkansas">Arkansas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Arkansas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Because of Gustav\'s slow motion across northwest Louisiana and Arkansas on September 4 and September 5, significant rainfall accumulation was seen statewide. The maximum amount in Arkansas was at <a href="/wiki/Hamburg,_Arkansas" title="Hamburg, Arkansas">Hamburg</a>, where 11.25 inches (286\xc2\xa0mm) had fallen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> making Gustav the third wettest tropical cyclone to affect the state since 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_implications">Political implications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Political implications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_3">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Hurricane Gustav was expected to make landfall near New Orleans almost exactly three years after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> struck the same region. It also arrived in the midst of the campaign for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 U.S. presidential elections</a> and during the week the <a href="/wiki/2008_Republican_National_Convention" title="2008 Republican National Convention">2008 Republican National Convention</a> was scheduled to start. The federal and state administrations, as well as the candidates for the 2008 presidential election were sensitive that Gustav was likely to remind U.S. voters of the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina_disaster_relief" title="Hurricane Katrina disaster relief">"botched response" by state and local municipalities and subsequent federal aid authorities</a> to the earlier storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On August 30, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and Vice President <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> canceled their planned attendance at the 2008 Republican National Convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bush_skips_RNC_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bush_skips_RNC-144">[144]</a></sup> Because of the expected U.S. landfall, governors and some other political leaders from Louisiana and other states chose to stay home from the 2008 Republican National Convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJGOPCHANGE_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJGOPCHANGE-145">[145]</a></sup> As the hurricane approached the coast, presumptive Republican presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> canceled all non-essential opening-day festivities at the convention<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCain_RNC_cancellations_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCain_RNC_cancellations-146">[146]</a></sup> and said that he might give his acceptance speech via satellite from the affected area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politico_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-politico-147">[147]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Democratic presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and Vice Presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, monitoring the situation in the Gulf Coast, encouraged New Orleans residents to evacuate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Obama also announced that he would ask his large network of donors and volunteers to contribute money, goods and work to assist victims of the storm according to what was most needed after the storm hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Louisiana\'s Congressional primary election, originally scheduled for September 6, was delayed to October 4, which then delayed the general election for two races that required a runoff vote to December 6, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_3">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> addressed in a "reflection," published on September 1 in the official daily <i><a href="/wiki/Granma_(newspaper)" title="Granma (newspaper)">Granma</a></i>. "Two days ago <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/..." title="...">...</a> out of 11 international press reports devoted to Cuba, none told about the hurricane that moved toward our island and the feverish efforts of our Civil Defense," Castro writes. Instead, the news services, "echoing a Yankee press organization dedicated to the media war and campaigns against Cuba," reported about the defection of TV actor <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yamil_Jaled&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yamil Jaled (page does not exist)">Yamil Jaled</a>. (The "Yankee press organization" appears to be an allusion to <i><a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Herald" title="El Nuevo Herald">El Nuevo Herald</a></i>, which broke the news of Jaled\'s arrival in Miami.) "What a patriot! What a democrat! What a brilliant example," wrote Castro. "This way, the world is informed about a character a lot less known and important than Hurricane Gustav. They want to make a sacred cow out of him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>\n<p>Because of the damage and deaths, on April 22, 2009, the name <i>Gustav</i> was retired by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>. It will never again be used to name an atlantic Hurricane again. It was replaced with Gonzalo which was first used in <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gonzalo" title="Hurricane Gonzalo">2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Gustav&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals"
